kTwqSL"></div></div> <div class="sc-fzbaOV cmDPyq"><div class="sc-dxQKuT eXyyNk"><div class="sc-efIWVM epnEGB"><div class="sc-ddGHkk soffp sc-bDzeIK hyVlcn"><div class="sc-hzyFKJ eHKwxF"><div class="sc-zlfrG jLFdhj"><h2 class="sc-cHqXqK sc-cgxxSg bTsuQr hdHryl">About Dataset</h2></div></div></div><div class="sc-dubKuk jIXXas"><div class="sc-irsnjx MsWUA"><div style="min-height: 80px;"><div class="sc-ePpfBx hvYpEH sc-hhNevu kAEMHr"><h3>Context</h3>
<p>Web sever logs contain information on any event that was registered/logged. This contains a lot of insights on website visitors, behavior, crawlers accessing the site, business insights, security issues, and more.  </p>
<p>This is a dataset for trying to gain insights from such a file. </p>
<h3>Content</h3>
<p>3.3GB of logs from an Iranian ecommerce website zanbil.ir.</p>
<h3>Acknowledgements</h3>
<p>Zaker, Farzin, 2019, "Online Shopping Store - Web Server Logs", <a rel="noreferrer nofollow" aria-label="https://doi.org/10.7910/DVN/3QBYB5 (opens in a new tab)" target="_blank" href="https://doi.org/10.7910/DVN/3QBYB5">https://doi.org/10.7910/DVN/3QBYB5</a>, Harvard Dataverse, V1</p>
<h3>Inspiration</h3>
<p>Trying to create an efficient pipeline for reading, parsing, compressing, and analyzing web server log files. </p></div></div></div></div></div><div class="sc-byEwEB dvRGed"><div class="sc-igFWaW
